  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_9acc5db4-a6e4-43e0-a42c-0dc891f8047c'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

           <span class="uitext reviewText">people who've read the rest of the series</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Shovelmonkey1 by: </span>
      books 1-3 demanded that the fourth was read

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer219299936" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15232975130972227632">Do you remember that bit in the Scream movie where Stu Macher (played by Matthew Lillard), turns to all the other film geeks and sets out the now famed set of rules for surviving a horror film and making it into the sequel? (FYI those rules were: Never have sex. Do not drink and never say “i’ll be right back”)<br/><br/>Well someone should be writing a similar set of rules for the characters in the Song of Fire and Ice Series because, oh boy are these guys in trouble. Despite the numerous sellswords, hedge</span>
  <span id="freeText15232975130972227632" style="display:none">Do you remember that bit in the Scream movie where Stu Macher (played by Matthew Lillard), turns to all the other film geeks and sets out the now famed set of rules for surviving a horror film and making it into the sequel? (FYI those rules were: Never have sex. Do not drink and never say “i’ll be right back”)<br /><br />Well someone should be writing a similar set of rules for the characters in the Song of Fire and Ice Series because, oh boy are these guys in trouble. Despite the numerous sellswords, hedge knights, rogues, assassins, Sers and Lords running about the place in full armour and with more oversized silverware and valerian steel than the kitchen department at John Lewis, no one is more fearsome in the culling stakes than George RR Martin himself. Watch out Westeros, Wildlings beyond the wall and everyone in the Land Beyond the Sea... Martin has the biggest axe and no one can stop if from falling.... or knows where it might fall next!<br /><br />Once again, this review will be scant on detail as it is impossible to discuss one iota of this epic without giving the game away and creating civil unrest amongst a legion of George RR Martin fans in the making. So... here’s what has happened so far:<br /><br />XXXXX is dead<br />And so is XXXXX<br />XXXXX has been poisoned<br />Ooh and so was XXXXX but they had it coming really and the only tears you’d want to shed in their direction are Tears of Lys.<br />XXXXX is mortally wounded and so is XXXXX although probably it would only be a matter of time before the killed each other anyway. <br />XXXXX and XXXXX are both dead too.<br />XXXXX is also gone to the grave. XXXXX went to the grave and then came back.<br />And XXXXX, XXXXX, XXXXX, XXXXX, XXXXX, XXXXX, XXXXX, XXXXX, XXXXX, XXXXX, XXXXX, XXXXX, XXXXX, XXXXX, XXXXX, XXXXX, XXXXX, XXXXX, XXXXX, XXXXX, XXXXX, XXXXX, XXXXX, XXXXX all died in various battles but they were mostly just lesser characters with walk on/carried off parts anyway.<br />XXXXX died on the toilet.<br /><br /> None of them will be making it into the sequel unless they’re getting a free pass to Wight world.<br /><br />XXXXX and surprisingly XXXXX are still alive. So is XXXXX. <br />XXXXX and XXXXX are on the run. XXXXX has become an unlikely ally. XXXXX and XXXXX are at the wall. The XXXXX has turned up and so has XXXXX. No one seems to be looking for XXXXX and XXXXX is out of sight and out of mind and growing in strength. <br /><br />So, how do you learn to duck, quick enough and low enough to avoid the George RR Martin cull? <br /><br />1.	Don’t offer to be a king, appoint yourself as king or have any claim to any throne or kingdom anywhere. There are a lot of kings around at the moment too but believe me, there is no safety in numbers.<br />2.	Don’t be a hero. <br />3.	Don’t be a coward either.<br />4.	Don’t treat with sellswords<br />5.	Don’t become a born again religious convert.<br />6.	Don’t be jealous.<br />7.	Don’t be coveteous.<br />8.	Don’t be related to any Starks.<br />9.	Don’t be related to any Lannisters.<br />10.	Don’t be in possession of anything that either the Starks, Lannisters, Tullys, Freys, Boltons, Baratheons, Targaryens, Florents, Redwynes, Umbers, Flynts, Fossoways, Kettlebacks, Ostermonts, Karstarks, Mollens, Talharts, Glovers, Seaworths, Greyjoys, Slynts, Celtigars, Cerwyns or Marbrands want.<br /><br />In short there is very little you can do in order to make it into the sequel. Maybe your safest option would be to take the black? <br /></span>

  <span id="freeText5945374174292689602" style="display:none"><i>“Night’s King was only a man by light of day...but the night was his to rule. And it’s getting dark.”</i><br /><br />This one is definitely a game changer! The war for the iron throne is ongoing but it seems being away from the battle can be just as deadly as fighting in it! <br /><br /><i>“It was not for murder that the gods punished him...but for slewing a guest under his roof; that the gods cannot forgive.” </i><br /><br />I am loving this series! All the action that is happening at the same time to the different characters in different areas is so addictive! I love seeing how the characters interlink - and I fear for what will happen to them all next! <br /><br />Arya is about to head off across the water after escaping numerous brigands, Sansa has found new troubles in a new place, Bran keeps on travelling, Davos still fights on for Stannis despite his Red Priestess, Brienne has fulfilled part of her vow and is off to fulfill the rest. Jaime is changed from his time with Robb and Catelyn, Tyrion’s family issues just get worse! Jon and Sam are having their own problems on the wall, far removed from all those in the South. Daenerys is conquering the East city by city. And where is Theon Greyjoy? <br /><br />Bring on A Feast for Crows!<br /><br /><i>“We are puppets dancing on the strings of those who came before us, and one day our own children will take up our strings and dance on in our stead.”</i></span>

  <span id="freeText10708111260881358376" style="display:none">Oh my bloody hell and fuck...<br /><br />Dear George,<br /><br />I have read A Game of Thrones, A Clash of Kings, and A Storm of Swords one after another and in any spare moment over the last couple of months. As a result, I think that this reality is starting to take over. My emotional involvement in the lives of your characters is reaching an unhealthy depth, and your brutality with them is breaking my motherfucking heart. I just finished ASOS a moment ago, and said motherfucking heart is beating some serious drum and bass. I often do and recently have read books to love, admire, and learn from. But dang dawg, I don't remember the last time reading was so damn EXCITING. I have NO IDEA what you're going to do or where you're going to take me next - all bets are off, because your world is a real one, where heroes get savaged and baddies prevail and shit happens that leaves you staring at the heavens and thinking WHAT DOES IT ALL MEAN?<br /><br />You're MAD. A mad marvellous genius and I love you. But I kind of hate you. Because you are KILLING me and I am becoming an obsessed crazy person.<br /><br />Shattered but scintillated,<br />Alex</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13941900627627815031">This is the ending that book three should have had. The first half, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/768889.A_Storm_of_Swords_Steel_and_Snow__A_Song_of_Ice_and_Fire__3__Part_1_of_2_' title='A Storm of Swords Steel and Snow (A Song of Ice and Fire #3, Part 1 of 2) by George R.R. Martin' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Storm of Swords: Steel and Snow</a>, just wasn't strong enough to stand on its own. But that's okay as the second half more than makes up for it. From the off, there are bodies. Not just secondary characters either, but people we thought were going to be key players in The Game.<br/><br/>A number of characters get built out a lot more as well.   <span id="freeText13941900627627815031" style="display:none">This is the ending that book three should have had. The first half, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/768889.A_Storm_of_Swords_Steel_and_Snow__A_Song_of_Ice_and_Fire__3__Part_1_of_2_" title="A Storm of Swords Steel and Snow (A Song of Ice and Fire #3, Part 1 of 2) by George R.R. Martin" rel="nofollow noopener">A Storm of Swords: Steel and Snow</a>, just wasn't strong enough to stand on its own. But that's okay as the second half more than makes up for it. From the off, there are bodies. Not just secondary characters either, but people we thought were going to be key players in The Game.<br /><br />A number of characters get built out a lot more as well. Jamie continues his transition to three-dimensions with the start of a conscience. Stannis starts to come out of his shell a little and Petyr's role in the history so far starts to make a lot more sense – he did warn us not to trust him!<br /><br />As a combined single book it would have been a five star rating, as part two more than rescues any failings in part one. I strongly suggest reading them back to back, and thinking of them as one logical book, if you're going to buy them individually.</span>

  <span id="freeText9703641265108577146" style="display:none"><b>I DON'T EVEN KNOW HOW TO BEGIN TO REVIEW THIS BOOK.</b> I NEED TO CRY FIRST. SQUALL ACTUALLY, LIKE A MURDERED ZUCCHINI BECAUSE OMG. SO NOT OVER.<br /><br />*pause for a moment to thank and hug and scream in horror at Engie who got me started on these books*<br /><br />Ahem. I'm good now. <br /><br />So usually I go through the narrators and give a quick recap on my feelings for them. SO I'LL DO THAT. Although I reviewed A Storm of Swords in TWO PARTS so you can see <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1319443960" rel="nofollow noopener">my review of PART ONE here</a>. <br /><br /><b>JAIME:</b> Maaaaybe just one of my most favouritest people ever. ;') Brienne and his relationship is THE BEST aND I SHIP IT. I don't ship Jaime/Cersei so hard anymore. Cersei is so focused on her kids she just walks over EVERYONE including Jaime. Omg, I'm so sad. I <i>did</i> ship them though...so you can see how far I've fallen. -_-<br /><b>TYRION:</b> Of course I love Tyrion. I ADORE HIM. HE WENT TOTAL PSYCHO BY THE END THOUGH. OMG. But I still love him and don't really feel bad for <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Tywin or Shae. Omg, I can't BELIEVE Shae betrayed him. That totally gutted Tyrion. I'm so so sad. And Tywin? I like TV!Show!Tywin better. He's just horrible in the books sadly. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><b>SANSA:</b> I feel SO SORRY FOR HER, but I still love her. I love how she's getting a lot more smarter and savvy, but she's <i>only thirteen years old, </i> AHHHHHH. Poor little poppet. Petyr is a total pervert though and every second that he's around Sansa makes me freak out.<br /><b>ARYA:</b> I...I feel awful about saying this but as MUCH as I love Arya's attitude and epicness, her chapters often get boring. I do like her character development and my heart keeps breaking every time she's sooo cloooose to being saved and then SO FAR. I have mixed feelings when she ends up with the Hound. I kind of wished he'd started teaching her sword play and stuff? But he didn't. What a let down.<br /><b>JON:</b> AWK JON MA DARLING. I cried, of course, when <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Ygritte <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> died, but but but I really REALLY badly wanted Jon to be made a Stark. SO BADLY. I also want Jon for King of the Universe.<br /><b>DANEYRS</b>: I felt she wasted a lot of time. She sacked cities and I ADORED how she did the whole "I'm a silly little girl and don't know anything" and then -- bOOM -- smites a city. And I LOVED the plot twist with Jorrah. I never liked Jorrah. Shady dude who's like in his 40s kissing a 16 year old? Not okay. Also Selme. I LIKE SELME.<br /><b>SAMWELL:</b> I looove Sam's chapters! I love his little crush on Gilly. And I adore how he's so matured and gotten stronger. Craven? HA. He does so so much manipulating in the last chapter in his soft, squishy trembling way IT'S JUST AMAZING. <br /><b>Catelyn:</b> OH CATELYN. Poor thing, she was so so tired and sad. <br /><b>Bran:</b> DEFINITELY the most boring narrator of ever. I'm so disappointed in Bran's chapters. Half the time he was just having Jojen and Mira telling old tales and stuff and WHOOO CAAAAARES when in King's Landing all this STUFF is going down. Gah.<br /><b>Davos:</b> Stilll. NOPE. I don't care about Davos. But his chapters were important and I'm glad he finally stood up to Stannis, the iron donkey.<br /><br />OKAY BUT LEMME JUST QUICKLY LIST THE DEATHS:<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />+ Catelyn: murdered at the Red Wedding and had her body dumped in the river BUT MABYE SHE'S A ZOMBIE ACCORDING TO THE EPILOGUE?? I MEAN. OMG.<br />+ King Robb: dead and murdered by the Freys at the Red Wedding along with like 90% of his men.<br />+ Joffery: poisoned at his own wedding feast by Lady Olenna and Sansa's hairnet. CHOKED ON PIE.<br />+ Lysa: pushed out of the Sky Window by Petyr. Totally saw that coming.<br />+ Red Viper/Obrynn: killed fighting The Mountain in a battle to save Tyrion from being beheaded for NOT killing Joffery.<br />+ Ygritte: killed while taking the wall, dies in Jon's arms. Lemme cry too.<br />+ Catelyn's father: died of old age I guess? Who even cares.<br />+ Balon Greyjoy: I think this was a biiiiit anti-climatic. He totally slips and FALLS OFF A SIDEWALK. Like. What.<br />+ Twyin: Murdered on the toilet by Tyrion. Can't say I'm crying. <br />+ Shae: murdered by choking by Tyrion when he found her in Tywin's bed. I get that she was forced, but still not really crying.<br /><br />Also The Hound was "left to die" when Arya just left him with huge wounds after he killed Polliver and The Tickler. And The Mountain is PROBS dying. And the Wilding King, Mans Raider, is also probably going to be executed.<br /><br />SO MANY SHOCKING DEATHS. I EXPECTED ROBB TO DIE, BUT NOT CATELYN. AND I CRIED AT OBERYNN  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>It was just non-stop brilliance the WHOLE TIME AND I LOVED IT.</b> It's my favourite book. Did I mention that?! and I'm sooo obsessed. Like I literally am always thinking about it and I can't wait to sit down and devour 2 seasons of the show! I love the character development. I love how NO ONE is safe. I love how it tears out my Vulcan heart and I feeeel aaaall the awful things. Wait. Did I say I loved that? I TOTALLY HATE IT BUT STILL. I'm still a fan of the Lannisters, even though they're like melon heads. And I LOVE Tyrion a lot, and Jon so so much. I guess they'll die soon. OMG. I'm so not handling all the deeeaths. And the size of teh world?! I JUST LOVE HOW IT KEEPS GETTING BIGGER AND BIGGER. And while I felt A Clash of Kings was totally just rabbiting along, I think A Storm of Swords NEVER let the tension slide. Perfection.<br /><br />Okay. I need to go, eh, drown myself in chocolate or something and then start bk 4 straight away.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9703641265108577146" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText3107655963225701056" style="display:none">A Storm of Swords: Steel and Snow (A Song of Ice and Fire #3, Part 2 of 2), George R.R. Martin<br />A Storm of Swords is the third of seven planned novels in A Song of Ice and Fire, a fantasy series by American author George R. R. Martin. It was first published on August 8, 2000, in the United Kingdom,[1] with a United States edition following in November 2000. Its publication was preceded by a novella called Path of the Dragon, which collects some of the Daenerys Targaryen chapters from the novel into a single book.<br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: از دوازدههم تا بیست و هشتم ماه می سال 2015 میلادی<br />عنوان: طوفان شمشیرها کتاب دوم از جلد 3 (نغمه آتش و یخ، #3)؛ نویسنده: جورج آر. آر. مارتین؛ مترجم: رویا خادم الرضا؛ مشخصات نشر: تهران، ویدا، 1393، در 789 ص، و دو ص نقشه، شابک: 9786002910752؛<br />طوفان شمشیرها سومین کتاب از مجموعه رمان فانتزی حماسی: ترانه یخ و آتش، اثر نویسنده آمریکایی: جرج آر. آر. مارتین است. در حال حاضر این کتاب طولانی‌ترین کتاب مجموعه است. با توجه به طولانی بودن کتاب در برخی کشورها از جمله استرالیا این کتاب به دو بخش تقسیم شده و به چاپ رسیده است. چکیده: داستان طوفان شمشیرها کمی پیش از داستان کتاب پیشین است. هفت پادشاهی هنوز درگیر جنگ پنج شاه هستند. شاه‌ های باقی‌مانده راب استارک، بالون گری‌جوی، جوفری باراتئون و استانیس باراتئون برای حفظ قدرتشان در جنگ برای حفظ موقعیت خودشان هستند. جنگ داخلی مردم عادی را از بین می‌برد. این داستان از دید ده شخصیت اصلی گفته می‌شود و یک پیش‌ مقدمه و یک شخصیت پس مقدمه هم دارد که در کل دوازده گوینده داستان حضور دارند. راویان: پیش مقدمه چت برادر و نگهدارنده سگها؛ سر جیمی لنیستر پسر بزرگ تایوین لنیستر برادر تیریون لنیستر؛ جان اسنو پسر حرام زاده ادارد استارک؛ بانو کتلین استارک؛ تیریون لنیستر؛ سانسا استارک؛ آریا استارک؛ برن استارک؛ سمول تارلی؛ سر داووس سی‌ورس؛ ملکه دنریس تارگرین؛ پس مقدمه: مرت فری؛ ا. شربیانی</span>

I will not ruin it for anybody, but this book turned me into an emotional reck in the best and worse possible ways. It gave me moments were I found myself jumping round like a child who actually did get a pony for christmas, moments when I bawled like a baby and finally, moments when I was yelling my head off, threatening to never read another page and swearing like a banshee.   <span id="freeText7197884022028440597" style="display:none">My favourite book of the series so far! I will not ruin it for anybody, but this book turned me into an emotional reck in the best and worse possible ways. It gave me moments were I found myself jumping round like a child who actually did get a pony for christmas, moments when I bawled like a baby and finally, moments when I was yelling my head off, threatening to never read another page and swearing like a banshee. This series needs to form part of everyone's life - it is so unpredictable and engrossing that it has to be up there with the greats.</span>

<div id="review_314546728" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/314546728" />
    <a title="Kirstine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5172557-kirstine"><img alt="Kirstine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1505503603p2/5172557.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/314546728?book_show_action=true">Apr 18, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kirstine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kirstine" href="/user/show/5172557-kirstine">Kirstine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5172557-kirstine?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5172557-kirstine?shelf=1-men">1-men</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5172557-kirstine?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer314546728" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9119117948689854533">AT LAST I SEE THE LIGHT!<br/><br/>Allow me to finally applaud you, George R.R. Martin without apprehension or dissatisfaction, without a hint of weariness or disappointment. Allow me to finally pass beyond the "<b>I want to love it, but I don't</b>" into "<b>I was swept away by fire and ice and I ascend now as a different woman</b>". <br/><br/><u>My favourite things about this book:</u><br/>1) Jon Snow's every move (the light of my heart)<br/>2) Jaime's journey to discover morals, honor and true love<br/><br/>Now, I can't tell you what it was about this i</span>
  <span id="freeText9119117948689854533" style="display:none">AT LAST I SEE THE LIGHT!<br /><br />Allow me to finally applaud you, George R.R. Martin without apprehension or dissatisfaction, without a hint of weariness or disappointment. Allow me to finally pass beyond the "<b>I want to love it, but I don't</b>" into "<b>I was swept away by fire and ice and I ascend now as a different woman</b>". <br /><br /><u>My favourite things about this book:</u><br />1) Jon Snow's every move (the light of my heart)<br />2) Jaime's journey to discover morals, honor and true love<br /><br />Now, I can't tell you what it was about this installment that finally did it. I have absolutely no clue why I have found the past three books so tedious to get through while this one passed by as easy as breathing. <br /><br />That most of the current plot lines culminated, crashed and made way for new ones was definitely a major influence. <i>A Game of Thrones</i> would have been brilliant if I hadn't watched the show first, but it suffered a bit from too many character introductions and too little happening. <i>A Clash of Kings</i> was chaos and confusion and a shitload of pain. <i>A Storm of Swords pt. 1</i> was no better, but with nothing happening for the first 300 pages and some of the chaos bleeding through from ACoK it wasn't exactly <b>thrilling</b>, it was mostly just a mess of characters and plots and whatnot. <br /><br /><b>This</b>, however, this is the book I've been waiting for. This is the reason I persisted and struggled through the others. <br /><br />This is where I finally come face to face with the greatness that you've all been babbling about, but that I had yet to see. <br /><br />This is in many ways the conclusion to the events that followed the execution of Ned Stark, which makes it a more pleasant read, because instead of throwing us more plotlines again and again and again, it actually <i>explains</i> some of it. It doesn't whirl the characters about, and throws them into rocks with sand in their eyes, it manages to <i>ground</i> them a bit instead.<br /><br />(When I say "pleasant" I, of course, don't mean to imply it will not cause you emotional pain and take a few stabs at your soul.)<br /><br />Still, those who have to die, die (and there aren't exactly few), those who don't, grieve and survive. And through it they all seem to find their feet a little better in this new world, even with the scales shifting and the balance thrown. They've gone from being lost creatures to having some resemblance of purpose - and just like the characters, the story has also grown and matured.<br /><br />I still don't give much of a damn about Dany - and a few of the other characters, shh -, she's a great character and all, but until I am told what purpose she serves for the story, I'm gonna continue not giving a damn. I can't help it, she's over there, everyone else is over here and I won't care until her dragons are huge and can carry her across the sea.<br /><br />Let's see if this experience will repeat itself with the next books or if I have to wait three books again. Oh well, if I have to, I will. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9119117948689854533" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14033928246121204641">Seven hells...what did I just read?😱🐺<br/><br/>A Storm of Swords or as I call it the wedding book is by far the best book in the series ASOIAF!<br/>Long yes, but for those of you who have watched or heard about the series this book describes the events we have watched both in season 3 and 4 ! Though, I have to say I have read about things they never showed us in the series(YET?) and I'm not talking about about small details, I'm talking about major stuff...Well I can't say anymore without spoiling something..B</span>
  <span id="freeText14033928246121204641" style="display:none">Seven hells...what did I just read?😱🐺<br /><br />A Storm of Swords or as I call it the wedding book is by far the best book in the series ASOIAF!<br />Long yes, but for those of you who have watched or heard about the series this book describes the events we have watched both in season 3 and 4 ! Though, I have to say I have read about things they never showed us in the series(YET?) and I'm not talking about about small details, I'm talking about major stuff...Well I can't say anymore without spoiling something..But the epilogue left me speechless!<br /><br />I couldn't find the full edition of the 3rd book so I bought part 1 and part 2. Due to their length it felt like reading 2 books so it was pretty obvious to me that the first part (abt 600 pages) was not so action-packed as I expected, so I gave it 4 stars. But boy, the second part was like 10 stars!<br />Like I said there are a lot of weddings described in this book and I personally hate weddings but these were really something! Master Martin makes sure you will cry, laugh, even bite your nails while reading this book. I think I have said that before, but I really love the fact that each chapter is told through a different character each time so we get a deeper insight into our beloved heroes while viewing the events from their perspective! Jaime appears to be a major character now, there's a lot being narrated from his point of view, but if I am not mistaken this is Arya's book! Her journey becomes even more treacherous and difficult and strangely enough it seems that most of the events revolve around her. I best liked Tyrion, Bran and Jaime-Brienne chapters!<br /><br />I really don't know what else to say!!! I can't wait to get my hands on the next book! <br /><br />Fantasy lovers enjoy!!!</span>

    <a title="✨    jamieson   ✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7706640-jamieson"><img alt="✨    jamieson   ✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499961431p2/7706640.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=2020-reads">2020-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=series-to-complete">series-to-complete</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=owned-books">owned-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=series">series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2332554738" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1221682744339752111"><i>
  <blockquote>“In King’s Landing, there are two sorts of people. The players and the pieces.”<br/></blockquote>
</i><br/><br/>A Storm of Swords is responsible for so many of the now-iconic moments from Game of Thrones. The Red Wedding, The Purple Wedding, <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ Tyrion's trial and Tywin's death, Oberyn Martell and Gregor Clegane's fight, Daenerys conquering of the cities, especially Astapor <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and so much more. <br/><br/>So it's not surprising this is such a well-loved instalment of the series. I do have to agree with the mas</span>
  <span id="freeText1221682744339752111" style="display:none"><i>
  <blockquote>“In King’s Landing, there are two sorts of people. The players and the pieces.”<br /></blockquote>
</i><br /><br />A Storm of Swords is responsible for so many of the now-iconic moments from Game of Thrones. The Red Wedding, The Purple Wedding, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Tyrion's trial and Tywin's death, Oberyn Martell and Gregor Clegane's fight, Daenerys conquering of the cities, especially Astapor <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and so much more. <br /><br />So it's not surprising this is such a well-loved instalment of the series. I do have to agree with the masses and say this is the best of the ASOIAF books so far. <br /><br />The first half is excellently plotted with meticulous character and political arcs, and the second half is a whirlwind of action and drama that undermines expectations over and over. Sam and Davos are extremely boring but, beside their chapters, I genuinely loved every POV included in this book and every character and plot arc. AND THAT EPILOGUE !!<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“You are grown so very great now, yet the higher a man climbs the farther he has to fall.”</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />And onto A Feast for Crows! Who knows when I'll get to it, though. I like that this is a world I can easily jump in and out of. I did have a lot of fun with this though, and I'll be looking forward to seeing what comes next (especially since I believe we're getting to the point where the book and show start to really deviate)<br /></span>

  <span id="freeText5007922825674942019" style="display:none">Possibly the most devastating, awesome, exciting and surprising instalment yet, and I'm starting to get a sneaking suspicion that the real story is only just starting...<br /><br />If you'd told me during the first book that by this point I would be pinning all of my hopes on The Hound and Jaime freaking Lannister, of all people, I'd have thought you were certifiable. But that would appear to be where we are at the moment, with Jaime in particular evolving into being one of the more interesting characters.<br /><br />Containing a ton of gruesome deaths it's now quite clear that absolutely no character is safe in this story, and I'm really enjoying being taken along on the remaining characters stories. I can only begin to imagine what may happen now with Arya possibly on her way to a reunion with Jaqen, Jon commanding the Wall and Tyrion having, awesomely, killed Tywin Lannister.         <a title="Sonja ✧･ﾟ｡★*☾" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sonja ✧･ﾟ｡★*☾" href="/user/show/35853271-sonja">Sonja ✧･ﾟ｡★*☾</a>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35853271-sonja?shelf=favourite">favourite</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35853271-sonja?shelf=awesomesauce">awesomesauce</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35853271-sonja?shelf=too-many-feels">too-many-feels</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1165860415" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15598493646449666447"><b>
  <blockquote>"Always keep your foes confused. If they are never certain who you are or what you want, they cannot know what you are like to do next."</blockquote>
</b>This book is pure genius. It made me wince in pain when a few of my favourite characters were murdered. It made me dizzy with joy when my most despised and hated character was murdered. And it made me feel all the little things in between during the whole span of <i>A Storm of Swords</i>.<b>
  <blockquote>"Weddings have become more perilous than battles, it would seem."</blockquote>
</b>I loved t</span>
  <span id="freeText15598493646449666447" style="display:none"><b>
  <blockquote>"Always keep your foes confused. If they are never certain who you are or what you want, they cannot know what you are like to do next."</blockquote>
</b>This book is pure genius. It made me wince in pain when a few of my favourite characters were murdered. It made me dizzy with joy when my most despised and hated character was murdered. And it made me feel all the little things in between during the whole span of <i>A Storm of Swords</i>.<b>
  <blockquote>"Weddings have become more perilous than battles, it would seem."</blockquote>
</b>I loved the way <i>A Storm of Swords: Blood and Gold</i> surprised me. I never expected people to die in the manner they did. I love the fact that even though <i>so many people</i> die it still hurts. George R.R. Martin makes me feel too many feels while reading. One moment I think the characters are safe and the tone is light and happy, and the next moment: everybody is dead.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1430998623ra/14785814.gif" width="250" height="160" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <b> All men must die.</b><br><br>One thing that I absolutely <i>loved</i> about this book was the character development! I learned a lot about the characters' backstories, intentions and true feelings. I started liking Jaime more and more as I continued reading. And Sandor Clegane as well.<b>
  <blockquote>"which is more dangerous, the dagger brandished by an enemy, or the hidden one pressed to your back by someone you never even see?"</blockquote>
</b> I love the way treachery is portrayed in the book. The reader is shown the intricate and delicate ways people can play the Game of Thrones. In <i>A Storm of Swords</i> I got a better insight on the way people try to manipulate and control each other to win the Game of Thrones. <b>
  <blockquote>"Smoke, sweat, and shit. King's Landing, in short. If you have a good nose you can smell the treachery too."</blockquote>
</b><br><b>
  <u>A Song of Ice and Fire (Book Reviews)</u>
</b><br><b>1.</b> <i>A Game of Thrones</i>: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1077696775?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">5 Great First Stars</a><br><b>2.</b> <i>A Clash of Kings</i>: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1122064421?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">5 Royal Stars</a><br><b>3.1</b> <i>A Storm of Swords Pt. 1</i>: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1165853003?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener"> 5 Red Stars</a><br><b>4.</b> <i>A Feast for Crows</i>: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1122064452?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener"> 5 Westerosi Stars</a></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1830249473" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5496510691231503661"><b> WHAT IN THE NAME OF SEVEN BLOODY HELLS DID I JUST READ? </b><br/><br/>This book is <i>phenomenal</i>. Full of stabbing, gutting, betrayal and a lot. There is bloody battle everywhere. What would happen if there is a war?   <span id="freeText5496510691231503661" style="display:none"><b> WHAT IN THE NAME OF SEVEN BLOODY HELLS DID I JUST READ? </b><br /><br />This book is <i>phenomenal</i>. Full of stabbing, gutting, betrayal and a lot. There is bloody battle everywhere. What would happen if there is a war? Just imagine.<br /><br />Every character has grown a lot but how long would they live, we don’t know. Now I know why George R.R Martin is well known for the characters death. Simply can’t explain my bloody love for this book. I was disappointed with its first part, but man this book surpassed all my expectations and raised my hope for the next book, the size of the wall. I’m pleased to say that this book is the best book(part) so far. Every page will suck you right into it. The secrets revealed, the broken trust and backstabbing, you will feel everything in your gut. You couldn’t guess a single bloody thing, your guess will always go into a poof. When you thought that something bad is going to happen, the worst will happen.<br /><br />There was not a single soul in this book considered to be happy. They were tested, tortured and were broken brutally. But still, they stood. I will not entrust myself to live in the Westeros. I wouldn’t even last a single bloody day. This book is <b> BRUTAL </b>, from The Red Wedding to the last bloody line. Everything captivated me. This is what I want from a book. And now I’m already in search for other similar stories, so that once I finished this series I’ll know where to go. <br /><br />Everything was planned brilliantly, we should definitely appreciate the mastermind behind the masterpiece.<br /><br />I want one thing. <i>Just a single damn thing</i>. Is it so wrong to ask? I just want the reunion of Starks. The family doesn’t need the throne and yet they were thrown into the Hunger Games. <br /><br />Characters:<br /><br /><b>Robb</b>: I don’t think he had my attention. But I know how honorable he was as his father. He is naturally a King. But if ONLY his heart wasn’t blinded by the beauty, surely the worse wouldn’t have happened. And I really want to admit this: I see Ned through him.<br /><br /><b>Sansa</b>: I always get irritated at her from the start. But this book made me pity her. I feel so sorry for her. I hope she will do something at least for her family name. Wolves. What I really wished is that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Joffrey could’ve been killed by Sansa. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Bran</b>: Not so much happened with him. But I really wished he could’ve met Jon in person at least once. He is a poor child, but trying to be brave for the prince sake. He is trying so hard. *sobbing*<br /><br /><b>Jon</b>: I was disappointed with him. Because he had Ygritte. I thought at least he has the honor when he said his vows. I can understand why he did that. It has to be done. However, my heart couldn’t accept it. What if he was a bastard? Was every bastard treacherous? It’s so bad when they accused him of being turn cloak.<br /><br /><b>Arya</b>: OMG! She was captured by someone every single time. She is brave. Fear cuts deeper than the sword. And I love every time when she said names before sleeping. <br /><br /><b>Jaime</b>: My hatred feelings towards him completely took a 360-degree turn. I love him. I shouldn’t have shipped him with Cersei. Yeah, I know. Fool’s play. I realized the mistake when Jaime was back at King’s Landing. He respected Brienne. That’s the thing everyone wants from a man. He hated the wench and yet respected her courage and stood with her. I was amused by his wits.<br /><br /><b>Cersei</b>: I HATE HER BLOODY GUTS. No more words.<br /><br /><b>Tyrion</b>: How he hate her sweet sister! For that alone, I love him more. Everyone thinks so low of him. I wonder what he would do if he came face to face with the one who framed him.<br /><br />Last but not least.<br /><br /><b>Dany</b>: I LOVE HER. She is fierce but easily broken. Blindly trusting everyone. She was gathering her own bloody army with her three dragons. That scores everything. I’m waiting for Dany to come to Westeros. It would be stunning. God, can’t wait. I was scoffing when some people believed that a single dragon could win the bloody war. Dude, wait and watch. Dany was coming with her THREE dragons. She will win the throne. I’m rooting for her.<br /><br /><b> <i> AMAZING READ! </i> </b><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5496510691231503661" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1925131879" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1925131879" />
    <a title="Omar Fadel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45226134-omar-fadel"><img alt="Omar Fadel" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1925131879?book_show_action=true">Sep 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Omar Fadel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Omar Fadel" href="/user/show/45226134-omar-fadel">Omar Fadel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/23516307-a-storm-of-swords">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45226134-omar-fadel?shelf=english">english</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1925131879" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1426903196628404482"><i>"A day will come when you think you are safe and happy, and your joy will turn to ashes in your mouth. And you will know the debt is paid."</i><br/><br/>This volume is the second part of the third of A Song of Ice and Fire and it is definitely the most powerful and page-turning part, by far. Full of fire and blood and really amazing character development. Unlike the first three volumes, I never felt bored or annoyed in any POV chapters. Of course I loved some more than others, but I can't deny that all were b</span>
  <span id="freeText1426903196628404482" style="display:none"><i>"A day will come when you think you are safe and happy, and your joy will turn to ashes in your mouth. And you will know the debt is paid."</i><br /><br />This volume is the second part of the third of A Song of Ice and Fire and it is definitely the most powerful and page-turning part, by far. Full of fire and blood and really amazing character development. Unlike the first three volumes, I never felt bored or annoyed in any POV chapters. Of course I loved some more than others, but I can't deny that all were better than they've ever been, except for Arya.<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>And who, are you, the proud lord said<br />that I must bow so low.</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />The events start in both sides of the Seven Kingdoms with preparations of two weddings. In King's Landing, the Lannisters and the Tyrells prepare for the marriage of King Joffrey with Margaery Tyrell. The guests arrive from everywhere in the Seven Kingdoms, among them Prince Oberyn Martell, Prince of Dorne with his paramour to attend the royal wedding. While in the North, Robb Stark, Catelyn Stark and Edmure Tully are on their way to reach Lord Walder Frey and attend Edmure's wedding at the Twins. Both weddings end tragically with very strong plot-twists - not to me, unfortunately - that really did change the cords of the Game. <br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>Only a cat with a different coat,<br />that's all the truth I know.</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />A Lannister always pays his debts. You'll be certain of this most of all all. Jaime, after finally preparing to return to King's Landing with one hand, says farewell to Brienne and departs. Then realizes he left something behind and get back to save Brienne. That chapter was really interesting. At King's Landing, they did not know him at first. They still call him “Kingslayer” and “Oathbreaker”. However, he returns to the Kingsguard, where no one sees him as an icon of honor. He also notices his weakness in using swords because his sword hand was cut, and he was not as good in using the left. Jaime’s chapters in this volume were not as rich as they were in Book Three: Steel and Snow. You can say this is when the things are settled for him. I really admired his relationship with Tyrion, how he loves him and stand against his sister and lover when it comes to his brother. <br /><br />Lord Tywin Lannister is still oppressing Tyrion and treating him badly as ever. But this book really takes his malicious hatred to a next level. Tyrion is now married to Sansa and commanded by his father to have her with child, in order to take the North should Robb Stark die, but of course he did not want to hurt her because she’s just a child. For the first time I see that Tyrion really loves Shae, and I used to think he is a fool. But the past is so terrible, and his father’s hatred to him is the reason behind all that, behind his love for whores. The trial of course is probably the best speech of Tyrion’s in all the entire series, when he confesses his guilt of being a dwarf.<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>In a coat of gold, or coat of red,<br />A lion still has claws.</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />After Beric Dondarrion fought the Hound and died, then resurrected, he believed that he is not guilty, took his gold and let him go. Arya considered him a traitor who cares about nothing but gold, and escaped. The Hound found her and decided to make use of her. Arya Stark's chapters in both volumes of <i>A Storm of Swords</i> are action-less compared to her fabulous adventures with Needle and Syrio Forell in <i>A Game of Thrones</i> or in Harrenhall with Jaqen H'ghar in <i>A Clash of Kings</i>. Yet her adventures with the Hound in this volume were so satisfying. <br /><br />Sansa - I don’t want to talk much about her because the interesting part is full of spoilers. She just has the intention to escape with Ser Dontos in Joffrey’s royal wedding with Margaery Tyrell while everybody is distracted.<br /><br />For the first time since I started reading books, I cried. Reading Catelyn’s last chapter made me feel really depressed although I knew what’ll happen. She is so strong and wretched and can do anything for the sake of her children.<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>And mine are long and sharp, my lord,<br />as long and sharp as yours.</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />Across the Narrow Sea, Daenerys reaches the city of Yunka'i and declares war on them, after her cunning trick in Astapor and her gaining the Unsulied army. They call her <i>Mhysa</i> now, <i>Mother, Mother of Dragons</i>. But that was not the part I liked, nor that one of Daario Naharis. In Khaleesi's POV chapters, I liked the part when she discovers two traitors in her company, one of them was one of her most trusted and faithful knights and how she deals with them.<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>And so he spoke, and so he spoke,<br />that lord of Castamere.<br />And now the rains weep o’er his halls,<br />And no one there to hear.</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />Jon Snow returns almost safe to the Night Watch. He tells them about his hardships and his dangerous adventures with the wildlings and the King Beyond the Wall. Some accuse him of being a traitor and a turnclock, some call him “Oathbreaker” and very few believe him. Jon Snow is not aware of the fate that awaits him, the King that awaits.<br /><br />One of my new favorite chapters were Samwell Tarly’s who I used to hate him in <i>Steel and Snow</i>, but this volume has definitely a very strong character development for him. <br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>Yes now the rains weep o’er his halls,<br />And not a soul to hear.</blockquote>
</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="1426903196628404482" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review213788588">

  <span id="freeText8351868035411082157" style="display:none">It seems like everything went wrong for everyone in this epic conclusion of A Storm of Swords; The Lannisters 'won' the war but still, they suffered from maiming, deaths, and betrayals. <br /><br />I absolutely enjoyed this one as I had the previous installments. It seemed to me as if the writing got better, which is weird because the writing has been consistently great throughout. Maybe I am just enjoying the series more and more with each volume?<br /><br />Once more, I do not find Jon's chapters as riveting as the others but I am thankful he is not in the snow most of the time but is actually in Westeros.<br /><br />I enjoyed Jamie's chapters, love Brienne and of course, Arya is my favorite. I still hate Sansa but I enjoyed her chapters. Dany's chapters were few but each time it was her turn to be presented to the reader I got sooooo excited. I love the woman she has become!<br /><br />I am such a huge Martin fan!! Already on A Feast of Crows.</span>

All of the seeds he has planted in the first two books have grown into cut-throat plots and killer conclusions. Martin's writing style is still dry, but the trials he puts his characters through made me forget that <i>A Storm of Swords</i> isn't perfect. This is the first volume of the Song of Ice and Fire series that I managed to read in little over two weeks - usually these take me at least a few months. My favourite book in the ser</span>
  <span id="freeText13657171863712610540" style="display:none">It has taken a while, but Martin's world is finally in its maturity. All of the seeds he has planted in the first two books have grown into cut-throat plots and killer conclusions. Martin's writing style is still dry, but the trials he puts his characters through made me forget that <i>A Storm of Swords</i> isn't perfect. This is the first volume of the Song of Ice and Fire series that I managed to read in little over two weeks - usually these take me at least a few months. My favourite book in the series so far.</span>

<div id="review_2074581657" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2074581657" />
    <a title="lydia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43905585-lydia"><img alt="lydia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529260823p2/43905585.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2074581657?book_show_action=true">Aug 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="lydia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="lydia" href="/user/show/43905585-lydia">lydia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/11539233-a-storm-of-swords">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2074581657" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3329646427338014627"><b>“Jaime Lannister sends his regards.”</b><br/><br/>Simply genious. This book is composed of political intrigue, cunning lords, unexpected alliances, heart-breaking betrayals and shocking battles- in a nutshell everything that makes <i>A Song of Ice And Fire</i> one of the best fantasy series ever. George R.R. Martin is an expert in plot twists and here he puts his talent in good use; you’ll never see the next death coming.<br/><br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[Also, you might want to avoid weddings after that. <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <span id="freeText3329646427338014627" style="display:none"><b>“Jaime Lannister sends his regards.”</b><br /><br />Simply genious. This book is composed of political intrigue, cunning lords, unexpected alliances, heart-breaking betrayals and shocking battles- in a nutshell everything that makes <i>A Song of Ice And Fire</i> one of the best fantasy series ever. George R.R. Martin is an expert in plot twists and here he puts his talent in good use; you’ll never see the next death coming.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Also, you might want to avoid weddings after that. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('F/ABLpeEjzRnBDnYWuZofBVE5sc2rxS3w48TrjhVXCxEuV7XFiswqUtG7NB9Icu16qhjPQowhNif+lXSGHL3qQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

and the incredible achievements of their advanced and imaginative society.\n\nAs Leick convincingly shows, Mesopotamian antiquity has as much interest as, and even greater importance than, Egypt; and       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/346732.George_R_R_Martin">About George R.R. Martin</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/346732.George_R_R_Martin"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_111x148-e08b4682eea7088f8cdfd67c131d51cd.png);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/346732.George_R_R_Martin">George R.R. Martin
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
96,727
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13678957883661317932">George Raymond Richard "R.R." Martin was born September 20, 1948, in Bayonne, New Jersey. His father was Raymond Collins Martin, a longshoreman, and his mother was Margaret Brady Martin. He has two sisters, Darleen Martin Lapinski and Janet Martin Patten. <br/><br/>Martin attended Mary Jane Donohoe School and Marist High School. He began writing very young, selling monster stories to other neighborhood chil</span>
  <span id="freeText13678957883661317932" style="display:none">George Raymond Richard "R.R." Martin was born September 20, 1948, in Bayonne, New Jersey. His father was Raymond Collins Martin, a longshoreman, and his mother was Margaret Brady Martin. He has two sisters, Darleen Martin Lapinski and Janet Martin Patten. <br /><br />Martin attended Mary Jane Donohoe School and Marist High School. He began writing very young, selling monster stories to other neighborhood children for pennies, dramatic readings included. Later he became a comic book fan and collector in high school, and began to write fiction for comic fanzines (amateur fan magazines). Martin's first professional sale was made in 1970 at age 21: "The Hero," sold to Galaxy, published in February, 1971 issue. Other sales followed. <br /><br />In 1970 Martin received a B.S. in Journalism from Northwestern University, Evanston, Illinois, graduating summa cum laude. He went on to complete a M.S. in Journalism in 1971, also from Northwestern. <br /><br />As a conscientious objector, Martin did alternative service 1972-1974 with VISTA, attached to Cook County Legal Assistance Foundation. He also directed chess tournaments for the Continental Chess Association from 1973-1976, and was a Journalism instructor at Clarke College, Dubuque, Iowa, from 1976-1978. He wrote part-time throughout the 1970s while working as a VISTA Volunteer, chess director, and teacher. <br /><br />In 1975 he married Gale Burnick. They divorced in 1979, with no children. Martin became a full-time writer in 1979. He was writer-in-residence at Clarke College from 1978-79. <br /><br />Moving on to Hollywood, Martin signed on as a story editor for Twilight Zone at CBS Television in 1986. In 1987 Martin became an Executive Story Consultant for Beauty and the Beast at CBS. In 1988 he became a Producer for Beauty and the Beast, then in 1989 moved up to Co-Supervising Producer. He was Executive Producer for Doorways, a pilot which he wrote for Columbia Pictures Television, which was filmed during 1992-93. <br /><br />Martin's present home is Santa Fe, New Mexico. He is a member of Science Fiction &amp; Fantasy Writers of America (he was South-Central Regional Director 1977-1979, and Vice President 1996-1998), and of Writers' Guild of America, West. <br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://us.macmillan.com/author/georgerrmartin">http://us.macmillan.com/author/george...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13678957883661317932" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
